# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

{"content":"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the Rust trait obligation chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've traced the complete trait obligation fulfillment chain in the Rust compiler (rust-lang/rust). The chain involves **11 key files** and **14 critical symbols** that work together to fulfill trait bounds during type checking.

### Key Components:

1. **ObligationForest** - Core data structure managing the forest of pending obligations
2. **FulfillmentContext** - Old trait solver's main wrapper around the obligation forest
3. **FulfillProcessor** - Implements obligation processing by invoking trait selection
4. **SelectionContext** - Central context for trait candidate selection and evaluation
5. **Candidate Assembly** - Collects all possible trait implementations
6. **Confirmation** - Verifies selected candidates and generates nested obligations
7. **Impl Matching** - MatchAgainstFreshVars matches impls against obligations
8. **TraitEngine** - Abstract trait defining the fulfillment engine interface
9. **Error Reporting** - Generates user-facing diagnostics for unresolved traits

### The Flow:

```
Obligation Registration
  ↓
ObligationForest.process_obligations()
  ↓
FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()
  ↓
SelectionContext.select()
  ↓
assemble_candidates() → evaluate_candidate() → best_candidate()
  ↓
confirm_candidate() + impl_matching
  ↓
Return subobligations or error
  ↓
Repeat until all obligations resolved
  ↓
report_selection_error() for any failures
```

**ObligationForest** data structure, which manages the forest of pending trait obligations. The chain represents the old (traditional) trait solver architecture, with a modern new solver implementation alongside it.\\n\\n### Core Components\\n\\n#### 1. ObligationForest (rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)\\nThe **ObligationForest** is the fundamental data structure that tracks outstanding trait obligations. It:\\n- Maintains a forest of obligation nodes, each with state (Pending, Waiting, Success, Error)\\n- Implements obligation dependency tracking with parent-child relationships\\n- Processes obligations via the `ObligationProcessor` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:268)\\n- Returns outcomes containing completed obligations and errors\\n- Caches processed results to avoid duplicate work\\n\\nThe forest uses three core result types defined by `ProcessResult<O, E>`:\\n- `Unchanged`: Ambiguous result, obligation stalled on type inference\\n- `Changed(Vec<O>)`: Obligation satisfied with subobligations\\n- `Error(E)`: Obligation failed\\n\\n#### 2. FulfillmentContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:61-104)\\nThe **FulfillmentContext** is the old trait solver's main context that manages trait fulfillment:\\n- Wraps an `ObligationForest<PendingPredicateObligation<'tcx>>`\\n- Implements the `TraitEngine` trait (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs:136)\\n- Registers obligations via `register_predicate_obligation()`\\n- Processes obligations through the `select()` method which invokes `FulfillProcessor`\\n- Snapshot-aware to ensure correct context usage\\n\\n#### 3. FulfillProcessor (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs:252-450)\\nThe **FulfillProcessor** implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait and:\\n- Processes each obligation in the forest by invoking trait selection\\n- Implements `needs_process_obligation()` with optimizations checking stalled inference variables\\n- Calls `SelectionContext.select()` for each obligation\\n- Generates sub-obligations from confirmed candidates\\n- Converts solver errors to fulfillment errors\\n\\n#### 4. SelectionContext (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs:104-126)\\nThe **SelectionContext** is the central context for trait candidate selection:\\n- Maintains inference context and freshener for trait predicates\\n- Tracks intercrate ambiguity causes for coherence checking\\n- Implements the selection algorithm via `select()` and `candidate_from_obligation()`\\n- Manages trait obligation stacks to detect cycles\\n- Caches selection results for performance\\n\\n#### 5. Candidate Assembly (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs:25-100)\\nThe **assemble_candidates()** method:\\n- Collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation\\n- Sources candidates from:\\n  - Trait aliases\\n  - User-defined impl blocks\\n  - Where-clause bounds\\n  - Built-in traits (Copy, Clone, Sized, etc.)\\n  - Projection predicates\\n- Returns a `SelectionCandidateSet` with definite and ambiguous candidates\\n\\n#### 6. Confirmation (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs:32-100)\\nThe **confirm_candidate()** method:\\n- Verifies that a selected candidate actually applies to the obligation\\n- Unifies trait reference type parameters\\n- Generates nested obligations based on the candidate type:\\n  - `ImplCandidate`: Calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` to generate where-clause obligations\\n  - `ParamCandidate`: Generates obligations from where-clause bounds\\n  - `BuiltinCandidate`: No nested obligations\\n  - `ObjectCandidate`, `ClosureCandidate`, etc.: Generate type-specific obligations\\n- Returns an `ImplSource` representing the selected implementation\\n\\n#### 7. Impl Matching (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs:24-117)\\nThe **MatchAgainstFreshVars** structure:\\n- Implements the `TypeRelation` trait to match types against fresh type variables\\n- Used to check if an impl's trait reference matches an obligation\\n- Approximates whether unification would succeed\\n- Returns Ok if match succeeds, Err if it fails\\n\\n#### 8. TraitEngine & ObligationCtxt (rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/engine.rs)\\nThe **TraitEngine** trait defines:\\n- `register_predicate_obligation()`: Adds obligations to the engine\\n- `try_evaluate_obligations()`: Processes pending obligations\\n- `report_fulfillment_errors()`: Reports errors for unfulfilled obligations\\n\\nThe **ObligationCtxt** provides a simpler API wrapper around TraitEngine.\\n\\n#### 9. Error Reporting (rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/)\\nError reporting occurs through:\\n- **report_selection_error()** (fulfillment_errors.rs:57-100): Main entry point for reporting trait errors\\n- **report_extra_impl_obligation()**: Reports obligations from impl items\\n- **on_unimplemented**: Custom error messages from #[diagnostic] attributes\\n- **suggestions**: Helpful suggestions for fixing trait errors\\n\\n### The Obligation Chain Flow\\n\\n1. **Registration**: Obligations registered via `ObligationCtxt.register_obligation()` \u2192 `TraitEngine.register_predicate_obligation()` \u2192 added to `FulfillmentContext.predicates` (ObligationForest)\\n\\n2. **Processing**: `FulfillmentContext.select()` calls `predicates.process_obligations(&mut FulfillProcessor)`\\n\\n3. **Obligation Processing**: `FulfillProcessor.process_obligation()` is called for each pending obligation\\n   - Checks if obligation needs processing via `needs_process_obligation()`\\n   - Calls `SelectionContext.select(obligation)`\\n\\n4. **Selection**: `SelectionContext.select()` \u2192 `candidate_from_obligation()` \u2192 `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`\\n   - Checks cache, calls `assemble_candidates()` to collect candidate implementations\\n   - Evaluates each candidate with `evaluate_candidate()`\\n   - Selects the best candidate (if any)\\n\\n5. **Confirmation**: Selected candidate is confirmed with `confirm_candidate()`\\n   - Unifies types and generates nested obligations\\n   - Returns `Selection` (impl source)\\n\\n6. **Result Processing**: `ProcessResult` returned to forest\\n   - `Changed(subobligations)`: Sub-obligations added to forest, parent suspended\\n   - `Unchanged`: Obligation stays pending for next iteration\\n   - `Error`: Obligation marked as error, backtrace recorded\\n\\n7. **Completion**: When all obligations resolved or errors detected, `process_obligations()` returns `Outcome` with completed obligations and errors\\n\\n8. **Error Reporting**: `report_selection_error()` called for unresolved errors, generating user-facing diagnostics\\n\\n### New Trait Solver\\n\\nIn parallel, the new trait solver (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/solve/) provides a modern implementation:\\n- Uses `FulfillmentCtxt` (different from old `FulfillmentContext`)\\n- Implements goal-based solving rather than obligation forest\\n- Used when `InferCtxt.next_trait_solver()` returns true\\n- Can be enabled with `-Znext-solver` flag\\n- Accessed through `InferCtxtSelectExt::select_in_new_trait_solver()`\\n\\nBoth solvers maintain the same public API through the `TraitEngine` trait, allowing for gradual migration.\"\n}\n",
